(2 comments)

I definitely think this automatic blocksize detection is a valuable optimization, and there have been attempts to do this for a long time.  I'm not yet convinced that this is the right implementation, but I'd be willing to accept that this is likely already much better than what is implemented today.  

Per my previous comments in LU-15963, it would make sense to include some timings from sanity test_398b (fio random write) with/without this patch into the commit comment to show the benefit.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2023-11-17 05:52:31.000000000) ---
Patch Set 35:

Brian, could you please review again.

It would be even better to confirm that e.g. a random 4KiB write workload to a file caused the file to keep a 4KiB blocksize, as this would avoid a ton of write inflation.

It probably wouldn't be hard to write a test case for this, something like:

        for BS in 4096 8192 16384 65536 131072; do
        for ((i = 0; i < 1024 * 1024 / BS; i++)); do
                dd if=/dev/urandom of=$DIR/$tfile.$BS bs=$BS count=1 seek=$RANDOM
        done
        (( $(stat -c %B $DIR/$tfile.$BS) == $BS )) || error "..."
        rm -f $DIR/$tfile.$BS
        done

I'm not sure if 'stat' on a ZFS-backed file from the client will return the *actual* blocksize.  This _might_ be tricky with multiple objects, but it should generally be consistent for a file.  It looks like osd-zfs/osd_object.c::osd_attr_get() is calling:

        sa_object_size(obj->oo_sa_hdl, &blksize, &blocks);

so I _think_ that is OK?
